<review>I visit Coachella Valley every couple of months as I have family here. A typical morning includes a hike or exercise followed by breakfast. I've noticed there are limited breakfast options in the valley.

However, Chula, as recommended, exceeded expectations. The coffee was fresh and fantastic, and I split three dishes with my mother and all were very delicious. The pozole with an added poached egg was a personal favorite. The frittata was my mothers personal favorite. The avocado toast was good, but I did not fully enjoy the sweet brioche (was it brioche?). I was expecting crispy sourdough for the avocado toast. Don't get me wrong it was still delicious but personal preference.

< review>
Almost never answers phone. Maybe they aren't open on Mondays, but I JUST called on Sunday to place a Monday order. They refused, said to call back tomorrow. I checked opening time with the person, she confirmed they'd open at 11:30am. No one's there, phone message box is full, the family member doing the pickup said the place was dark.

We loved this place, but the service is not good. They have a huge menu and often half the stuff isn't being served and/or it's reserved for dinner/weekends/whatever. The only reason I'm giving it two stars is that I quite like the food and staff when I can actually be there in person and they actually make what I ask for. It's like being in a terrible relationship you know you should end, and I sadly think I'll just have to walk away from this place. I've tried ordering out several times, and non-communication feels like they simply don't want customers. Good luck, Iccho.</review>

We went to Iccho Restaurant in Crenshaw to celebrate the bday celebration of our relative and we brought cake for him. The manager, Tomo, was so rude because he cannot let the cake we brought to be served. He insisted that they have to wash for the dishes and cut the cake and by doing that they will charge us! We told him that we can cut the cake ourselves and use our dirty dishes just to allow us to eat the cake because this cake is his favorite and they don't serve cake anyway. Whenever we went to any restaurant and bring cake we never encounter this kind of problem. Instead, they are so happy that we chose their restaurant to celebrate the birthday. Some even bring us free cake for the celebrant. But this place does not even have compassion and care for their customers. What are a couple of plates you lend for the cake of the celebrant? I ordered some high end led lights for my car & asked if they could do it since i heard that this shop specializes in headlight installations & of course they said yes. First impression walking in not to bad of a place some decent brand names here & there for parts, but back to the headlights it took them awhile (close to 3 hrs) to install it. No one acknowledges your existence for at least a few minutes. After 15 minutes, you're anointed with the blessing of their hipster attention. <Rating>4<//Rating><user>100056107176374195997<//user>< Text>
COVID Takeaways:
- Plenty of outdoor seating with social-distanced tables and plastic separators
- Takeout available (and super easy to pick up)
- Staff wear face coverings

The kalguksu and bossam here ARE TO DIE FOR!! I came here with 3 other people (so party of 4 total) and we ordered 1 kalguksu, 1 large bossam, and spicy rice cakes and we weren't able to finish everything. The prices seem a little steep, but portion sizes are huge. The food here, especially the kalguksu, is so comforting and hearty. I'd definitely go more frequently during colder days.

On the other hand, the parking in this plaza is terrible but it isn't the restaurant's fault. Cars have to park across of other cars, and you'd have to a note with your phone number on the front so the valet can call you if you have to move it. I recommend finding parking 30 minutes in advance of your meal.</Text>

Franccesco Freire< /user_name>
< Time>
1567816321300<//Time>
<Rating>3< /Rating>< text>
I usually rate places very unbiased, however..
When I think of pizza, the first few thoughts are Happy, Unison, Fresh. I really feel like this place was not any of the above. I went on Friday around 5 pm, and I wish I would have read a bit more about it. They essentially sell pizza by the slice/pie, however they have pizza sitting in an enclosure, half cooked it appears, and whenever you order, they pop it in a little oven and it re-heats it. Not really too fresh and the slices they had were limited. To be unbiased, I ordered a Vegan pizza (which was good for being vegan), along with another meat pizza. You could definitely taste the fact it was reheated, and it was particularly not my thing as it isnt very fresh. They also said they didn't have chicken wings and that they run out before the weekend, which is something they anticipate, so why not order more if you know your business is running out of a certain item?
The place had a weird aesthetic, (see pictures attached) and it was clean (mostly) but it didn't call out as Fresh, or a happy place. They also had not updated their menus that were printed which I see as an easy fix.
On a whole different topic, the staff was very friendly and very kind and patient.
I feel like this place has a great amount of potential and could bloom very well with fresh pizzas instead of re-heating a couple of slices and serving them.
I'm not unsatisfied with my experience, just somewhere I wouldn't personally visit again or recommend to others.</text>

<Rate>3< /Rate><Text>It's definitely a great NY pizza with good sauce, crust and cook. I do have issues with some of the experiences I've had. I've called in orders a few times and each time I'm treated like they are doing me a favor by taking my order. But it's not a big deal and the wife enjoys the pizza so I deal. But tonight I placed an order for a plain cheese pizza pickup and when I arrived they told me they had no orders for me and that I must have messed up and ordered from a different location. So it was my fault and they only offered to make an order now and I can wait for 25 mins for it to be finished. Well I check my phone and call the number that I had ordered from earlier and they answered, it WAS the same location!!  But still they are like we don't know what you're talking about since there are no orders here for you and again tell me I can wait for another pie to be made. Keep in mind they basically always have cheese pizza on hand because they sell it by the slice!  So why not just sell me one of the cheese pizzas??  Well I tell them to make me a new one and I go walk out to my car to tell my wife it's going to be 25 mins and then they call me. Apparently they had given my pizza to someone else with a completely different name and different order. He realized when he got to his car and brought the pizza back. So I wasn't crazy and had ordered from here, even though they acted like I was being the jerk!  So then the weird thing is they gave me that pizza that the other guy brought in, which I'm pretty sure is against health code. You can't sell food to a customer that another one has already walked out the door with!!  But whatever, I didn't wanna wait and they said they'd discount it. Except they didn't discount the pizza, they charged me $17 for a plain cheese pizza!  That's the normal price!!  Of course after all this by the time I got home the pizza was cold and chewy. Definitely not worth the hassle and frustration. I can't say I'll never go back, because the food is honestly good, but I probably won't be frequenting it because I just don't want to deal with sketchy service.<//Text><Pics>None</Pics>< resp>

Best pizza in North Park, definitely beats out Pizza Bruno and Sicilian Thing. I always and have only ordered a full Mona Lisa pie (their "supreme" version) for take-out. Thin, crispy, flavorful. They have good beers on tap ($6 for 2 slices and a beer), but I've never dined in. Frankly, the restaurant is pretty hot, and some of the servers at the counter can be assholes when it's busy.<//review>

The best pizza in San Diego! In a city where I find the pizza to be lacking, this place offers some fresh tasting, quality ingredients. Lots of unique pizzas, that have flavors I've never had before. Forgettable.

I came here as a going away lunch for coming back to college. My mom saw it on the food networks Diners, Drive In's, and Dives and it was just okay. There is a wide array of pizzas and combos that you can choose from. Many of them are very different from what you would normally order from a traditional pizza hut or papa johns so it was good in that sense, but i'm not sure if its just not my style or type of pizza, where they cook it and place it out then warm it back up when you order it. The prices are okay and the service is pretty much order and take to your seat. All in all i wouldn't choose to come back, but i'm always open for a good pizza.

Happy Hunting!< /review>
